      <p><b>Australia</b>, formally the <b>Commonwealth of Australia</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_hemisphere" title="Southern hemisphere">southern hemisphere</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> is <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>, and its largest city is <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>. </p>
      <p>Australia is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_area" title="List of countries by area">sixth biggest country in the world</a> by land area, and is part of the <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasian</a> regions. Australia, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> and other islands on the Australian <a href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="Tectonic plate">tectonic plate</a> are together called <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a>, which is one of the world's great <a href="/wiki/Ecozone" title="Ecozone">ecozones</a>. When other Pacific islands are included with Australasia, it is called <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>. </p>
      <p>25 million<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> people live in Australia, and about 85% of them live near the east coast. <sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> The country is divided up into six <a href="/wiki/States_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="States of Australia">states</a> and two territories, and more than half of Australia's <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> lives in and around the cities of <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Western_Australia" title="Perth, Western Australia">Perth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>. </p>
      <p>Australia is known for its <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a> (coal, iron, gold, diamonds and crystals), its production of <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>, and as the world's largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Emblem" title="Emblem">emblem</a> is a flower called the Golden Wattle. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:As-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/As-map.png/220px-As-map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8c/As-map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="353"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:As-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Australia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia's landmass of 7,617,930 square kilometers is on the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Australian_Plate" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Australian Plate">Indo-Australian plate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> The continent of Australia, including the island of Tasmania, was separated from the other continents of the world many millions of years ago. Because of this, many <a href="/wiki/Animals" class="mw-redirect" title="Animals">animals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Plants">plants</a> live in Australia that do not live anywhere else. These include animals like the <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo" title="Kangaroo">kangaroo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Koala" title="Koala">koala</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Emu" title="Emu">emu</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kookaburra" title="Kookaburra">kookaburra</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Platypus" title="Platypus">platypus</a>. </p>
      <p>People first arrived in Australia more than 50,000 years ago. These native Australians are called the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Aborigine" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Aborigine">Australian Aborigines</a>. For the history of Australia, see <a href="/wiki/History_of_Australia" title="History of Australia">History of Australia</a>. </p>
      <p>Most of the Australian colonies, having been settled from <a href="/wiki/Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Britain">Britain</a>, became mostly independent democratic states in the 1850s and all six combined as a federation on 1 January 1901. The first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Prime Minister of Australia</a> was <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Barton" title="Edmund Barton">Edmund Barton</a> in 1901. Australia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as Queen of Australia and Head of State and a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">Governor-General</a> who is chosen by the Prime Minister to carry out all the duties of the Queen in Australia. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions_and_cities">Regions and cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Regions and cities">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: Regions and cities">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="boilerplate seealso"><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cities_in_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Cities in Australia">List of Cities in Australia</a></i></span>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p>Australia has six states, two major mainland territories, and other minor territories. The states are <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> The two major mainland territories are the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory" title="Australian Capital Territory">Australian Capital Territory</a> (ACT). </p>
      <p>In 2013 according to world bank Australia had just over 23.13 million people. Most Australians live in cities along the coast, such as <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perth,_Western_Australia" title="Perth, Western Australia">Perth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Darwin, Australia">Darwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>. The largest inland city is <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>, which is also the nation's capital. The largest city is Sydney.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia is a very big country, but much of the land is very dry, and the middle of the continent is mostly <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>. Only the areas around the east, west and south coast have enough rain and a suitable <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> (not too hot) for many <a href="/wiki/Farm" title="Farm">farms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Cities">cities</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aboriginal_people">Aboriginal people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Aboriginal people">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Aboriginal people">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Corroboree.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Corroboree.jpg/220px-Corroboree.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/88/Corroboree.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="272" data-file-height="230"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Corroboree.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Photograph of Arrernte men of Central Australia in a <a href="/wiki/Corroboree" title="Corroboree">Corroboree</a> in 1900.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Aborigine" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Aborigine">Australian Aboriginal</a> people arrived in Australia about 50,000 years ago or even earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> Until the arrival of British settlers in 1788, the Aboriginal people lived by hunting and gathering food from the land. They lived in all sorts of climates and managed the land in different ways. An example of Aboriginal land management was the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cumberland_Plain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cumberland Plain (not yet started)">Cumberland Plain</a> where Sydney is now. Every few years the Aboriginal people would burn the grass and small trees.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> This meant that a lot of grass grew back, but not many big trees. Kangaroos like to live on grassy plains, but not in forests. The kangaroos that lived on the plain were a good food supply for the Aboriginal people. Sometimes, Aborigines would name a person after an animal, and they could not eat that animal to help level out the food population. </p>
      <p>Aboriginal people did not usually build houses, except huts of grass, leaves and bark. They did not usually build walls or fences, and there were no horses, cows or sheep in Australia that needed to be kept in pens. The only Aboriginal buildings that are known are fish-traps made from stones piled up in the river, and the remains of a few stone huts in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria, Australia">Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> The Aboriginal people did not use metal or make pottery or use bows and arrows or weave cloth. In some parts of Australia the people used sharp flaked-stone spearheads, but most Aboriginal spears were made of sharply pointed wood. Australia has a lot of trees that have very hard wood that was good for spear making. The <a href="/wiki/Boomerang" title="Boomerang">boomerang</a> was used in some areas for sport and for hunting. </p>
      <p>The Aboriginal people did not think that the land belonged to them. They believed that they had grown from the land, so it was like their mother, and they belonged to the land. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terra_Australis">Terra Australis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Terra Australis">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Terra Australis">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the 1600s, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> merchants traded with the islands of <a href="/wiki/Batavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Batavia">Batavia</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>), to the north of Australia and several different Dutch ships touched on the coast of Australia. The Dutch governor, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Van_Diemen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Van Diemen (not yet started)">van Diemen</a>, sent <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> on a voyage of discovery and he found <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, which he named <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land" title="Van Diemen's Land">Van Diemen's Land</a>. Its name was later changed to honour the man who discovered it. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="British Government">British Government</a> was sure that there must be a very large land in the south, that had not been explored. They sent Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. His ship, <i><a href="/wiki/HMS_Endeavour" title="HMS Endeavour">HMS Endeavour</a></i>, carried the famous scientists, Sir <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Banks" title="Joseph Banks">Joseph Banks</a> and Dr Solander who were going to <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a> where they would watch the planet <a href="/wiki/Venus_(planet)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venus (planet)">Venus</a> pass in front of the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>. Captain Cook's secret mission was to find "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Terra_Australis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Terra Australis (not yet started)">Terra Australis</a>" (the Land of the South). </p>
      <p>The voyage of discovery was very successful, because they found <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and sailed right around it. Then they sailed westward. At last, a boy, William Hicks, who was up the mast spotted land on the <a href="/wiki/Horizon" title="Horizon">horizon</a>. Captain Cook named that bit of land <a href="/wiki/Point_Hicks" title="Point Hicks">Point Hicks</a>. They sailed up the coast and Captain Cook named the land that he saw "New South Wales". At last they sailed into a large open bay which was full of fish and stingrays which the sailors speared for food. Joseph Banks and Dr. Solander went ashore and were astonished to find that they did not know what any of the plants or birds or animals that they saw were. They collected hundreds of plants to take back to England. </p>
      <p>Captain Cook saw the Aboriginal people with their simple way of life. He saw them fishing and hunting and collecting grass seeds and fruit. But there were no houses and no fences. In most parts of the world, people put up a house and a fence or some marker to show that they own the land. But the Aboriginal people did not own the land in that way. They belonged to the land, like a baby belongs to its mother. Captain Cook went home to England and told the government that no-one owned the land. This would later cause a terrible problem for the Aboriginal people. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Settlement">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Settlement">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove,_Jan._26th_1788.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg/220px-The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg/330px-The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg/440px-The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove%2C_Jan._26th_1788.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1026"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Founding_of_Australia._By_Capt._Arthur_Phillip_R.N._Sydney_Cove,_Jan._26th_1788.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Captain <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Phillip" title="Arthur Phillip">Arthur Phillip</a> raises the British flag at <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> in 1788.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1700s, in England, laws were tough, many people were poor and <a href="/wiki/Gaol" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaol">gaols</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jail" class="mw-redirect" title="Jail">jails</a>) were full. A person could be sentenced to death for stealing a loaf of bread. Many people were hung for small crimes. But usually they were just thrown in gaol. Often they were sent away to the British colonies in America. But by the 1770s, the colonies in America became the United States. They were free from British rule and would not take England's convicts any more, so England needed to find a new and less populated place. </p>
      <p>By the 1780s the gaols of England were so full that convicts were often chained up in rotting old ships. The government decided to make a settlement in New South Wales and send some of the convicts there. In 1788 the <a href="/wiki/First_Fleet" title="First Fleet">First Fleet</a> of eleven ships set sail from <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth" title="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</a> carrying convicts, sailors, marines, a few free settlers and enough food to last for two years. Their leader was Captain <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Phillip" title="Arthur Phillip">Arthur Phillip</a>. They were to make a new colony at the place that Captain Cook had discovered, named Botany Bay because of all the unknown plants found there by the two scientists. </p>
      <p>Captain Phillip found that <a href="/wiki/Botany_Bay" title="Botany Bay">Botany Bay</a> was flat and windy. There was not much fresh water. He went with two ships up the coast and sailed into a great harbor which he said was "the finest harbor in the world!" There were many small bays on the harbor so he decided on one which had a good stream of fresh water and some flat shore to land on. On 26 January 1788, the flag was raised and New South Wales was claimed in the name of <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a> of England, and the new settlement was called Sydney. </p>
      <p>For the first few years of the settlement, things were very difficult. No-one in the British Government had thought very hard about what sort of convicts should be sent to make a new colony. Nobody had chosen them carefully. There was only one man who was a farmer. There was no-one among the convicts who was a builder, a brick-maker or a blacksmith. No-one knew how to fix the tools when they broke. All of the cattle escaped. There were no cooking pots. All the plants were different so no-one knew which ones could be eaten. It was probable that everyone in the new colony would die of starvation. </p>
      <p>Somehow, the little group of tents with a hut for the Governor, Arthur Phillip, and another hut for the supply of food, grew into a small town with streets, a bridge over the stream, a windmill for grinding grain and wharves for ships. By the 1820s there was a fine brick house for the Governor. There was also a hospital and a convict barracks and a beautiful church which are still standing today. Settlements had spread out from Sydney, firstly to <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land" title="Van Diemen's Land">Van Diemen's Land</a> (Tasmania), and also up the coast to Newcastle, where coal was discovered, and inland where the missing cattle were found to have grown to a large herd. Spanish Merino sheep had been brought to Sydney, and by 1820, farmers were raising fat lambs for meat and also sending fine wool back to the factories of England. </p>
      <p>While the settlement was growing in New South Wales, it was also growing in Tasmania. The climate in Tasmania was more like that in England, and farmers found it easy to grow crops there. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration">Exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Exploration">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Exploration">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg/220px-Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg/330px-Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg/440px-Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="820" data-file-height="993"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ln-Governor-Lachlan_macquarie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Governor <a href="/wiki/Lachlan_Macquarie" title="Lachlan Macquarie">Lachlan Macquarie</a> was the 5th <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_South_Wales" title="Governor of New South Wales">governor of New South Wales</a> and one who though that Australia could be a rich and free place.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Because Australia is such a very large land, it was easy to think that it might be able to hold a very large number of people. In the early days of the colony, a great number of explorers went out, searching for good land to settle on. When the settlers looked west from Sydney, they saw a range of mountains which they called the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Mountains_(New_South_Wales)" title="Blue Mountains (New South Wales)">Blue Mountains</a>. They were not very high and did not look very rugged but for many years no-one could find their way through them. In 1813 <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Blaxland" title="Gregory Blaxland">Gregory Blaxland</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Lawson_(explorer)" title="William Lawson (explorer)">William Lawson</a> and a 17-year-old called <a href="/wiki/William_Charles_Wentworth" class="mw-redirect" title="William Charles Wentworth">William Charles Wentworth</a> crossed the Blue Mountains and found land on the other side which was good for farming. A road was built and the governor, <a href="/wiki/Lachlan_Macquarie" title="Lachlan Macquarie">Lachlan Macquarie</a> founded the town of <a href="/wiki/Bathurst,_New_South_Wales" title="Bathurst, New South Wales">Bathurst</a> on the other side, 100&nbsp;miles from Sydney. </p>
      <p>Some people, like Captain <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sturt" title="Charles Sturt">Charles Sturt</a> were sure that there must be a sea in the middle of Australia and set out to find it. Many of the explorers did not prepare very well, or else they went out to explore at the hottest time of year. Some died like Burke and Wills. <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Leichhardt" title="Ludwig Leichhardt">Ludwig Leichhardt</a> got lost twice. The second time, he was never seen again. Major <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mitchell" title="Thomas Mitchell">Thomas Mitchell</a> was one of the most successful explorers. He mapped the country as he went, and his maps remained in use for more than 100 years. He travelled all the way to what is now western Victoria, and to his surprise and annoyance found that he was not the first white person there. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Henty_Brothers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Henty Brothers (not yet started)">Henty brothers</a> had come from <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, had built themselves a house, had a successful farm and fed the Major and his men on roast lamb and wine. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self_government">Self government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Self government">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Self government">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The gold rushes of New South Wales and Victoria started in 1851 leading to large numbers of people arriving to search for gold. The population grew across south east Australia and made great wealth and industry. By 1853 the gold rushes had made some poor people, very rich. </p>
      <p>The transportation of convicts to Australia ended in the 1840s and 1850s and more changes came. The people in Australia wanted to run their own country, and not be told what to do from London. The first governments in the colonies were run by governors chosen by London. Soon the settlers wanted local government and more democracy. <a href="/wiki/William_Wentworth" title="William Wentworth">William Wentworth</a> started the Australian Patriotic Association (Australia's first political party) in 1835 to demand <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">democratic government</a>. In 1840, the city councils started and some people could vote. <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_Legislative_Council" title="New South Wales Legislative Council">New South Wales Legislative Council</a> had its first elections in 1843, again with some limits on who could vote. In 1855, limited self-government was given by London to New South Wales, Victoria, South Australia and Tasmania. In 1855, the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to vote">right to vote</a> was given to all men over 21 in <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>. The other colonies soon followed. Women were given the vote in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Australia" title="Parliament of South Australia">Parliament of South Australia</a> in 1895 and they became the first women in the world allowed to stand in elections.<sup id="cite_ref-aec.gov.au_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aec.gov.au-24">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australians had started parliamentary democracies all across the continent. But voices were getting louder for all of them to come together as one country with a national parliament. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Commonwealth_of_Australia">The Commonwealth of Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: The Commonwealth of Australia">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: The Commonwealth of Australia">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg/300px-Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg/450px-Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg/600px-Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="718"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_the_first_parliament.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A painting of the opening of the first <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Australia" title="Parliament of Australia">Parliament of Australia</a>, 9 May 1901, painted by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Roberts" title="Tom Roberts">Tom Roberts</a>. Australia has had democracy since the 1850s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG/300px-Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG" decoding="async" width="300" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG/450px-Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG/600px-Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_PR_COB_2006.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Countries of birth of Australian estimated resident population, 2006.
         <br>Source:Australian Bureau of Statistics<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Until 1901, Australia was not a <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">nation</a>, it was six separate <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colonies</a> governed by Britain. They voted to join together to form one new country, called the Commonwealth of Australia, in 1901. Australia was still part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, and at first wanted only British or Europeans to come to Australia. But soon it had its own money, and its own Army and Navy. </p>
      <p>In Australia at this time, the <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade union">trade unions</a> were very strong, and they started a political party, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Australian Labor Party</a>. Australia passed many laws to help the <a href="/wiki/Worker" title="Worker">workers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1914, the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> started in Europe. Australia joined in on the side of Britain against <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. Australian soldiers were sent to <a href="/wiki/Gallipoli_Campaign" title="Gallipoli Campaign">Gallipoli</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. They fought bravely, but were beaten by the Turks. Today Australia remembers this battle every year on <a href="/wiki/ANZAC_Day" title="ANZAC Day">ANZAC Day</a>. They also fought on the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Front">Western Front</a>. More than 60,000 Australians were killed. </p>
      <p>Australia had a really hard time in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> of the 1930s and joined Britain in a war against <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> when Hitler invaded Poland in 1939. But in 1941 lots of Australian soldiers were captured in the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Occupation_of_Singapore" title="Japanese Occupation of Singapore">Fall of Singapore</a> by Japan. Then Japan started attacking Australia and people worried about invasion. But with help from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>, the Japanese were stopped. After the war, Australia became a close friend of the United States. </p>
      <p>When the war ended, Australia felt that it needed many more people to fill the country up and to work. So the government said it would take in people from Europe who had lost their homes in the war. It did things like building the <a href="/wiki/Snowy_Mountains_Scheme" title="Snowy Mountains Scheme">Snowy Mountains Scheme</a>. Over the next 25 years, millions of people came to Australia. They came especially from <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, other countries in Europe. Later they also came from countries like <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>. An important new party, the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(Australia)" title="Liberal Party (Australia)">Liberal Party of Australia</a> was made by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Menzies" title="Robert Menzies">Robert Menzies</a> in 1944 and it won lots of elections from 1949 until in 1972, then <a href="/wiki/Gough_Whitlam" title="Gough Whitlam">Gough Whitlam</a> won for the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Labor Party</a>. Whitlam made changes, but he made the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Senate" title="Australian Senate">Senate</a> unhappy and the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">Governor-General</a> sacked him and forced an election in 1975. Then <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Fraser" title="Malcolm Fraser">Malcolm Fraser</a> won a few elections for the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal Party of Australia">Liberal Party</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 1960s many people began coming to Australia from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and other countries in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. Australia became more <a href="/wiki/Multicultural" class="mw-redirect" title="Multicultural">multicultural</a>. In the 1950s and 1960s Australia became one of the richest countries in the world, helped by mining and wool. Australia started trading more with America, than Japan. Australia supported the United States in wars against <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. Australian soldiers also helped the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in countries like <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> in 1999. </p>
      <p>In 1973, the famous <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Opera_House" title="Sydney Opera House">Sydney Opera House</a> opened. In the 1970s, 80s and 90s lots of <a href="/wiki/Australian_cinema" title="Australian cinema">Australian movies</a>, actors and <a href="/wiki/Australian_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian music">singers</a> became famous around the world. In the year 2000, <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">Sydney had the Summer Olympics</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 1980s and 90s, the Labor Party under <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hawke" title="Bob Hawke">Bob Hawke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Keating" title="Paul Keating">Paul Keating</a>, then the Liberal Party under <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a> made lots of changes to the economy. Australia had a bad <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a> in 1991, but when other Western countries <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_crisis_of_September%E2%80%93October_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Global financial crisis of September–October 2008">had trouble with their economies in 2008</a>, Australia stayed strong. </p>
      <p>Today Australia is a rich, peaceful and democratic country. But it still has problems. Around 4-5% of Australians could not get a job in 2010. A lot of land in Australia (like <a href="/wiki/Uluru" title="Uluru">Uluru</a>) has been returned to Aboriginal people, but lots of Aborigines are still poorer than everybody else. Every year the government chooses a big number of new people from all around the world to come as <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrants</a> to live in Australia. These people may come because they want to do business, or to live in a democracy, to join their family, or because they are <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a>. Australia took 6.5 million immigrants in the 60 years after <a href="/wiki/World_War_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="World War Two">World War Two</a>, including around 660,000 refugees.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Julia_Gillard" title="Julia Gillard">Julia Gillard</a> became the first woman <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Prime Minister of Australia</a> in 2010 when she replaced her colleague <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Rudd" title="Kevin Rudd">Kevin Rudd</a> of the Labor Party. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg/220px-Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg/330px-Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg/440px-Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_house_of_representatives04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The chamber of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_House_of_Representatives" title="Australian House of Representatives">Australian House of Representatives</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia is made up of six <a href="/wiki/State" title="State">states</a>, and two mainland <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/territory" class="extiw" title="wikt:territory">territories</a>. Each state and territory has its own <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">Parliament</a> and makes its own local <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">laws</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Australia" title="Parliament of Australia">Parliament of Australia</a> sits in Canberra and makes laws for the whole country, also known as the Commonwealth or <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">Federation</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">Federal</a> government is led by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Prime Minister of Australia</a>, who is the member of Parliament chosen as leader. The current Prime Minister is <a href="/wiki/Scott_Morrison" title="Scott Morrison">Scott Morrison</a>. </p>
      <p>The leader of Australia is the Prime Minister, although the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">Governor-General</a> represents the Queen of Australia, who is also the Queen of Great Britain, as head of state. The Governor-General, currently <a href="/wiki/His_Excellency" class="mw-redirect" title="His Excellency">His Excellency</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Hurley" title="David Hurley">David Hurley</a>, is chosen by the Prime Minister. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg/220px-Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg/330px-Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg/440px-Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3038" data-file-height="2012"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sydney_Opera_House_Night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <center>
          The <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Opera_House" title="Sydney Opera House">Sydney Opera House</a> was officially opened in 1973.
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia was <a href="/wiki/Colonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonisation">colonised</a> by people from <a href="/wiki/Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Britain">Britain</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> but today people from all over the world live there. English is the main spoken language, and Christianity is the main religion, though all religions are accepted and not everybody has a religion. Australia is <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multicultural</a>, which means that all its people are encouraged to keep their different languages, religions and ways of life, while also learning <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and joining in with other Australians. </p>
      <p>Famous <a href="/wiki/Australian_literature" title="Australian literature">Australian writers</a> include the bush balladeers <a href="/wiki/Banjo_Paterson" title="Banjo Paterson">Banjo Paterson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Lawson" title="Henry Lawson">Henry Lawson</a> who wrote about life in the Australian bush. More modern famous writers include <a href="/wiki/Peter_Carey_(novelist)" title="Peter Carey (novelist)">Peter Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Keneally" title="Thomas Keneally">Thomas Keneally</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colleen_McCullough" title="Colleen McCullough">Colleen McCullough</a>. In 1973, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_White" title="Patrick White">Patrick White</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>, the only Australian to have achieved this; he is seen as one of the great English-language writers of the twentieth century. </p> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Australian_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian music">Australian music</a> has had lots of world-wide stars, for example the opera singers <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Melba" title="Nellie Melba">Nellie Melba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joan_Sutherland" title="Joan Sutherland">Joan Sutherland</a>, the rock and roll bands <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">Bee Gees</a>, <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a> and <a href="/wiki/INXS" title="INXS">INXS</a>, the folk-rocker <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kelly_(musician)" title="Paul Kelly (musician)">Paul Kelly (musician)</a>, the pop singer <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australian_country_music" title="Australian country music">Australian country music</a> stars <a href="/wiki/Slim_Dusty" title="Slim Dusty">Slim Dusty</a> and John Williamson. <a href="/wiki/Australian_Aboriginal_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Aboriginal music">Australian Aboriginal music</a> is very special and very ancient: it has the famous <a href="/wiki/Digeridoo" class="mw-redirect" title="Digeridoo">digeridoo</a> woodwind instrument. </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Didgeridoo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Didgeridoo.jpg/220px-Didgeridoo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="35" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Didgeridoo.jpg/330px-Didgeridoo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Didgeridoo.jpg/440px-Didgeridoo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="840" data-file-height="133"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Didgeridoo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Didgeridoo" title="Didgeridoo">didgeridoo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australian TV has produced many successful programs for home and overseas - including <a href="/wiki/Skippy_the_Bush_Kangaroo" title="Skippy the Bush Kangaroo">Skippy the Bush Kangaroo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Home_and_Away" title="Home and Away">Home and Away</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neighbours" title="Neighbours">Neighbours</a> - and produced such well known TV stars as <a href="/wiki/Barry_Humphries" title="Barry Humphries">Barry Humphries</a> (<i>Dame Edna Everage</i>), <a href="/wiki/Steve_Irwin" title="Steve Irwin">Steve Irwin</a> (<i>The Crocodile Hunter</i>) and <a href="/wiki/The_Wiggles" title="The Wiggles">The Wiggles</a>. Major Australian subgroups such as the Bogan have been shown on Australian TV in shows such as <a href="/wiki/Bogan_Hunters" title="Bogan Hunters">Bogan Hunters</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kath_%26_Kim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kath &amp; Kim (not yet started)">Kath &amp; Kim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia has two public broadcasters (the ABC and the multi-cultural SBS), three commercial television networks, three pay-TV services, and numerous public, non-profit television and radio stations. Each major city has its daily newspapers, and there are two national daily newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian" title="The Australian">The Australian</a></i> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Australian_Financial_Review&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Australian Financial Review (not yet started)">The Australian Financial Review</a></i>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Australian_cinema" title="Australian cinema">Australian movies</a> have a very long history. The world's first feature movie was the Australian movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang" title="The Story of the Kelly Gang">The Story of the Kelly Gang</a></i> of 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> In 1933, <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Wake_of_the_Bounty" title="In the Wake of the Bounty">In the Wake of the Bounty</a></i>, directed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_Chauvel_(filmmaker)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Charles Chauvel (filmmaker) (not yet started)">Charles Chauvel</a>, had <a href="/wiki/Errol_Flynn" title="Errol Flynn">Errol Flynn</a> as the main actor.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> Flynn went on to a celebrated career in Hollywood. The first Australian Oscar was won by 1942's <i><a href="/wiki/Kokoda_Front_Line!" title="Kokoda Front Line!">Kokoda Front Line!</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Ken_G._Hall" title="Ken G. Hall">Ken G. Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> In the 1970s and 1980s lots of big Australian movies and movie stars became world famous with movies like <i><a href="/wiki/Picnic_at_Hanging_Rock" title="Picnic at Hanging Rock">Picnic at Hanging Rock</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Gallipoli_(1981_movie)" title="Gallipoli (1981 movie)"><i>Gallipoli</i></a> (with <a href="/wiki/Mel_Gibson" title="Mel Gibson">Mel Gibson</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_from_Snowy_River_(1982_movie)" title="The Man from Snowy River (1982 movie)">The Man From Snowy River</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Crocodile_Dundee" title="Crocodile Dundee">Crocodile Dundee</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russell_Crowe" title="Russell Crowe">Russell Crowe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">Cate Blanchett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heath_Ledger" title="Heath Ledger">Heath Ledger</a> became global stars during the 1990s and <i><a href="/wiki/Australia_(2008_movie)" title="Australia (2008 movie)">Australia</a></i> starring <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman" title="Nicole Kidman">Nicole Kidman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Jackman" title="Hugh Jackman">Hugh Jackman</a> made a lot of money in 2008. </p>
      <p>Australia is also a popular destination for business conferences and research, with Sydney named as one of the top 20 meeting destinations in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Sport">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: Sport">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DonaldBradman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/DonaldBradman.jpg/150px-DonaldBradman.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/DonaldBradman.jpg/225px-DonaldBradman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/42/DonaldBradman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="294" data-file-height="384"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DonaldBradman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Don_Bradman" class="mw-redirect" title="Don Bradman">Don Bradman</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sport is an important part of Australian culture because the climate is good for outdoor activities. 23.5% Australians over the age of 15 regularly take part in organised sporting activities.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> In international sports, Australia has very strong teams in <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, and performs well in <a href="/wiki/Cycling" class="mw-redirect" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rowing" title="Rowing">rowing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swimming" title="Swimming">swimming</a>. Local popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Australian_Rules_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Rules Football">Australian Rules Football</a>, horse racing, soccer and motor racing. Australia has participated in every summer <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> since 1896, and every <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>. Australia has hosted the <a href="/wiki/1956_Summer_Olympics" title="1956 Summer Olympics">1956</a> and <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a>, and has ranked in the top five medal-winners since 2000. Australia has also hosted the 1938, 1962, 1982 and 2006 <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> and are to host the 2018 Commonwealth Games. Other major international events held regularly in Australia include the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Open" title="Australian Open">Australian Open</a>, one of the four <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tennis tournaments, annual international cricket matches and the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> <a href="/wiki/Australian_Grand_Prix" title="Australian Grand Prix">Australian Grand Prix</a>. Corporate and government sponsorship of many sports and elite athletes is common in Australia. Televised sport is popular; some of the highest-rated television programs include the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a> and the grand finals of local and international football competitions. </p>
      <p>The main sporting leagues for males are the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">Australian Football League</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a>, <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_League_(Australasia)" title="National Basketball League (Australasia)">NBL</a>. For women, they are <a href="/wiki/ANZ_Netball_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="ANZ Netball Championships">ANZ Netball Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/W-League_(Australia)" title="W-League (Australia)">W-League</a> and <a href="/wiki/WNBL" class="mw-redirect" title="WNBL">WNBL</a>. </p>
      <p>Famous Australian <a href="/wiki/Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports">sports</a> players include the <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricketer</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Donald_Bradman" title="Donald Bradman">Donald Bradman</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Swimming" title="Swimming">swimmer</a> <a href="/wiki/Ian_Thorpe" title="Ian Thorpe">Ian Thorpe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sportsperson" title="Sportsperson">athlete</a> <a href="/wiki/Cathy_Freeman" title="Cathy Freeman">Cathy Freeman</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_festivals">Art festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Art festivals">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Art festivals">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Just 60 years ago, Australia had only one big art festival. Now Australia has hundreds of smaller community-based festivals, and national and regional festivals that focus on specific art forms.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Wildlife">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Change section: Wildlife">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Australia is home to many animals that can be found nowhere else on Earth, which include: the <a href="/wiki/Koala" title="Koala">Koalas,</a>the <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo" title="Kangaroo">Kangaroo</a>s, the <a href="/wiki/Wombat" title="Wombat">Wombat</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Numbat" title="Numbat">Numbat</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Emu" title="Emu">Emu</a>, among many others. Most of the <a href="/wiki/Marsupial" title="Marsupial">marsupials</a> in the world are found only on the continent. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Numbat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Numbat.jpg/220px-Numbat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Numbat.jpg/330px-Numbat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Numbat.jpg/440px-Numbat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="724"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Numbat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Numbat" title="Numbat">Numbat</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

In other contexts, the <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> of Australia, "<a href="/wiki/Advance_Australia_Fair" title="Advance Australia Fair">Advance Australia Fair</a>", is played.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span> </li>
